APPENDIX 4: STAKEHOLDER DESCRIPTION TABLE  
 
Stakeholder  Rights, interest, and overall relevance to the project 
Communities Project-zone village residents All communities residing in the 14 villages   within and/or adjacent to the 
project area, whose income, livelihoods, or cultural values are derived from 
the area, are collectively referred to as the project-zone communities. 
Groups Farmers Groups of people who make living through traditional farming (e.g., rice, corn 
and vegetables), agroforestry (such as rubber plantation and honey 
production) and raising animals such as chickens, pigs and cattle. Some of 
these groups are still practising shifting cultivation as well as slash and burn 
which can pose a threat to the project area.  
 Fishermen Groups of people who are dependent on rivers in the project area (i.e. 
Seluan River, Uluk Palin River, and Sibau River) a for a living through 
traditional fisheries and/or aquaculture.  
 Non-timber forest product 
(NTFP) collectors 
Groups of people who make a living by collecting non-timber forest products 
such as mushroom, honey, rattan, resin, kratom, medicinal plants, and more 
from the forested area of the project area. Additionally, they engage in the 
processing of rattan into handcrafted items such as hats, mats, baskets, 
bags, and kitchen storage, while also producing textiles from natural dyes 
and crafting mats from fibers like Purun.  
 Loggers Groups of people engaged in the extraction of commercial timber from the 
project area and selling logs to local communities based on demand. 
Additionally, some individuals utilize timber for personal use   

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
322 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
 Hunters Individuals or groups of people engaged in hunting wildlife from the project 
area (e.g. birds, deer, pigs) for consumption and/or to generate household 
income. 
 Marginalized Groups  Communities in the project area who are vulnerable due to factors such as 
disability, widowhood, or advanced age, which often result in social and 
economic marginalization. These groups typically face limited access to 
programs and services that could enhance their livelihoods, hindered by 
physical, geographical, or economic barriers. Moreover, they are frequently 
excluded from decision-making processes, with their needs and concerns 
neglected in local governance initiatives. 
Other stakeholders 
Central government Ministry of Forestry (BKSDA, 
TN Betung Kerihun, BPHL, 
BPKH, Manggala Agni) 
A central government authority responsible for formulating policies, 
overseeing and supervising forestry activities up to the provincial level, 
thereby shaping the project through regulatory frameworks and strategic 
cooperation. This project will engage in close collaboration with these 
agencies, ensuring seamless alignment with their mandates and 
institutional responsibilities. 
Local government Provincial Forestry 
Government (Dishut Provinsi, 
KPH) 
A provincial government entity charged with the implementation of forestry 
policies, management, and oversight, exerting influence on the project 
through policy guidance, technical support, and the monitoring of forestry 
activities. The project will pose no detrimental effects; rather, it will engage 
in close collaboration, reinforcing and aligning with the entity’s mandates 
and responsibilities. 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
323 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
 District Government (DLH, 
Dinas Pertanian, BPMDES, 
BPBD) 
A local government body at the municipal/regency level, functioning under 
the principle of autonomy, entrusted with the administration of regional 
affairs and accountable to the central government. This entity possesses the 
capacity to exert substantial influence on the project through its policy 
frameworks and regional development initiative, particularly within the 
sectors of agriculture, environmental stewardship, and community 
empowerment. The project will engage in constructive collaboration with this 
entity, ensuring alignment with its strategic and regional priorities. 
 Sub-district Government 
(Camat) 
The Sub-district head (Camat) serves as a liaison between the district 
government and village governments, overseeing matters related to 
development, village boundaries, inter-village conflict, and the supervision of 
village administration. In relation to the project, the Camat acts as a 
mediator between the company and the village governments, facilitating the 
resolution of issues, particularly those concerning project activities at the 
village level. The implementation of the project will have no adverse impacts 
on the sub-district authority but will instead foster constructive collaboration 
to ensure alignment with local governance structures. 
 Village Government (Pemdes, 
BPD, Bumdes) 
The Village Government (Pemdes) serves as the primary administrative 
authority at the village level, functioning as the local arm of both central and 
regional governments. It plays a pivotal role in implementing development 
initiatives and managing community affairs. Through its decisions and 
policies, Pemdes can directly shape project outcomes within the village. 
Supporting this structure, the Village Consultative Body (BPD) acts as a 
representative institution with legislative and oversight responsibilities, 
offering strategic value in drafting village regulations particularly those 
related to environmental protection and the prevention of illegal logging. 
Complementing these governance roles, the Village Owned Enterprise 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
324 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
(Bumdes) operates as an economic instrument to harness local potential, 
positioning itself as key partner in scaling and marketing community driven 
business initiatives. 
Customary Institution Dayak Customary Council 
(DAD)/Dewan Adat Dayak 
(DAD) 
The Dayak Customary Council is a traditional institution composed of 
representatives from various Dayak sub-ethnic groups across both district 
and provincial levels. Its role parallels that of customary institutions at the 
village and customary territory (ketemenggungan) levels, particularly in 
preserving cultural traditions, resolving conflicts through customary 
mechanisms, safeguarding customary lands, and serving as a bridge 
between local communities and the government. As the highest customary 
authority at the district and provincial level, the Dayak Customary Council 
may serve as a key mediator in addressing customary issues arising 
between the company and local customary institutions at the village or 
ketemenggungan level within the context of the project.  
 Regional Indigenous People / 
Ketemenggungan 
The Ketemenggungan is a customary institution overseeing multiple villages, 
holding greater authority than village-level customary bodies, particularly in 
matters of customary law and territorial rights. Its decisions carry significant 
weight for project activities within the concession area, which is traditionally 
recognized as part of its ancestral domain. 
 Village Indigenous People / 
Lembaga adat desa 
The village-level customary institution holds significant influence, serving to 
preserve traditional customs, resolve conflicts through customary law, 
safeguard ancestral territories, and act as a liaison between the community 
and the village government. Its decisions and customary laws, such as 
activity restrictions or customary sanctions can directly affect project 
operations within the concession area, which is regarded as part of 
ancestral land. The project has formally informed this institution that its 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
325 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
implementation will not cause adverse environmental impacts and will fully 
align with customary norms and regulations 
Non-Governmental 
Organizations (NGOs) 
Yayasan Sangga Buana Lestari 
 
A local NGO focused on environmental conservation and community 
development, actively supporting the establishment of Village Forests 
(Hutan Desa) and Customary Forests (Hutan Adat) in areas that may 
intersect with the Project Area. Should these proposals be approved, they 
would require careful coordination to ensure alignment with project 
boundaries and to support mutually respectful land management practices. 
 Taruna Tani Permata 
Khatulistiwa 
A youth-based organization engaged in sustainable agriculture, with a focus 
on promoting organic farming through hydroponics. It also supports 
hydroponic initiatives for women’s groups (PKK) at both district and village 
levels. Given its expertise, the organization presents strong potential for 
collaboration with the project’s supported farmer groups to advance eco-
friendly agriculture and enhance local livelihoods in line with the project's 
objectives. 
 PRCF Since 2016, PRCF (People Resources and Conservation Foundation) has 
played a key role in environmental conservation in Nanga Lauk Village. It 
established and continues to support the Village Forest Management 
Institution (LPHD), overseeing 1,430 hectares. PRCF provides capacity 
building for forest patrols to detect illegal activities, supports ecosystem 
rehabilitation, and promotes forest-based enterprises such as rattan, honey, 
and rubber. The foundation holds strong influence in Nanga Lauk through its 
institutional support, patrol team development, enterprise facilitation, and 
contribution to village-level regulations. In relation to the project, PRCF offers 
valuable opportunities for collaboration in forest monitoring, livelihood 
development, and regulatory strengthening at the village level. 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
326 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
 Aliansi Masyarakat Adat 
Kapuas Hulu (AMAKH) 
The Kapuas Hulu Indigenous Peoples Alliance (AMAKH) is part of the 
national AMAN network, which focuses on indigenous rights through policy 
advocacy, territorial mapping, and economic empowerment. AMAKH holds 
significant influence among indigenous communities in North Putussibau 
and has actively supported the establishment of customary forests in Banua 
Tengah, Nanga Nyabau, and Sungai Uluk Palin. 
 Bentang Kalimantan Tangguh Bentang Kalimantan Tangguh is a local NGO based in West Kalimantan, 
focusing on tropical forest conservation, sustainable natural resource 
management, and community empowerment. Although its operational areas 
do not overlap with the project’s concession villages, the organization holds 
influence in Kapuas Hulu on issues related to forest governance and carbon 
trading. In the context of the project, it may shape village government 
perspectives on carbon market mechanisms within the concession area. 
 Mananang Banua Mananang Buana is a youth organization legally constituted as an 
association, representing the young people of the Tamambaloh Apalin 
Ketemenggungan. The organization advocates for the establishment of 
village and customary forests in four villages (Sungai Uluk Palin, Nanga 
Nyabau, Banua Tengah, and Lauk). With significant influence within the 
indigenous community, local governments, and the residents of 
Tamambaloh, Mananang Buana is well-positioned to serve as a mediator or 
conciliator in resolving conflicts or issues in Nanga Nyabau, Sungai Uluk 
Palin, and Banua Tengah. 
Private Sector PT BIA A palm oil company in close proximity to the Project Area, whose activities, 
including the expansion of oil palm plantations by local communities 
partnered with the company, may impact the project.

 PT Harkat Luhur Ekosistem A PBPH operating near the project area, which could be seen as a potential

 Kalimantan Agro Lestari A palm oil company operating near the project area, particularly in North 
Putussibau District, which may impact the project through the expansion of 
oil palm plantation areas in several nearby villages, potentially altering land-
use patterns. 
 Keling Kumang Agro A cooperative-based enterprise specializing in livestock and agriculture, 
particularly in providing layers (egg-laying chickens) and feed, hybrid corn 
seeds, farming tools, and related training. Additionally, it serves as a buyer 
for products from its partners, such as eggs and corn. This organization may 
impact the project positively, especially through collaboration with local 
community business groups within the project zone.

Data / Parameter  FRSD|BSL 
Data unit  Dimensionless  
Description  Residual Stand Damage Factor  
Source of data  Pinards and Putz (1996) 
Value applied 2.30 
Justification  of  choice 
of  data  or  description 
of measurement 
methods and 
procedures applied  
No  specific  reference  is  available  on  the  Residual  Stand  Damage  Factor 
(RSD) for Indonesia case.  
Based on this reason, the RSD value applied in the calculation use the RSD 
value  of neighbouring country (Malaysia) as  studied by  Pinards and Putz  in 
1996.  The  similarity  in  the  context  of  forest  characteristic  and  logging 
practices  between  both  countries believed  to  be  relevant  to  ensure  the 
conservativeness of the calculation.  
Purpose of Data  Determination of baseline scenario  
Comments  - 
 
Data/ Parameter:  Vl,j,i,sp 
Data unit:  m3/ha

CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4

at typically 1.3 m aboveground level) and merchantable height (MH).

procedures (if any):

Any comment:  Merchantable Volume (V) is calculated by using formula commonly applied in 
timber concession in Indonesia as below: 
V= 1/4*DBH^2*MV* 0.6. The merchantable volume is calculated in unit of 
m3.  
The field data and calculation sheet is available at validation.  
As suggested by the methodology, the merchantable volume further analysed 
into two tree classes; Dipterocarpaceae and mixed tree species.

Data unit:  Kg kg-1

384 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
Used in equations:   
Description:  OF, SLF and WW are used for oxidation and the decay of wood product in IFM-
LtFP  
 
OF  =  Fraction  of  wood  products  that  will  be  emitted  to  the  atmosphere 
between 3 and100 years after production;  
SLF = Fraction of wood products that will be emitted to the atmosphere within 
3 years of production; and  
WW  =  Fraction  of  extracted  biomass  effectively  emitted  to  the  atmosphere 
during production  
 
Wood Waste fraction (WW):  
 
Winjum  et  al  (1998)  indicate  the  proportion  of  extracted  biomass  that  is 
oxidized  (burning  or  decaying)  from  the  production  of  commodities  for 
developing and developed countries.  
 
Short-lived fraction (SLF)  
Winjumetal1998  give  decay  rates  for  proportions  of  wood  products,  which 
were converted to with short-term (<3yr)  
 
Additional Oxidized Fraction (OF)  
Winjum  et  al  1998  gives  annual  oxidation  fractions  for  each  class  of  wood 
products.  
This gives the additional proportion that is oxidized between the 3rd and the 
100th.  
Source of data:  The source of data is the published paper of Winjum et al.199838  
Value applied: Wood Waste fraction (WW): 24% (for developing countries) 
 
Short-lived fraction (SLF)

Data / Parameter:  Project Forest Cover Monitoring Map  
Data Unit: Ha 
Description:  Map  showing  the  location  of  forest  land  within  the  project  area  at  the 
beginning of each monitoring period. If within the Project Area some forest 
land  is  cleared,  the  benchmark  map  must  show  the  deforested  areas  at 
each monitoring event  
Source of data:  Remote  sensing  in  combination  with  GPS  data  collected  during  ground 
truthing  
Justification of choice of 
data  or   description  of 
measurement  methods 
and procedures applied:  
The   minimum   map   accuracy   must   be   90%   for   the   classification   of 
forest/non-forest in the remote sensing imagery.  
If  the  classification  accuracy  is  less  than  90%  then  the  map  is  not 
acceptable  for  further  analysis.  More  remote  sensing  data  and  ground 
truthing  data  will  be  needed  to  produce  a  product  that  reaches  the  90% 
minimum mapping accuracy.  
Frequency: Must be monitored at least every 5 years or if verification occurs 
on a frequency of less than every 5 years examination must occur prior to 
any verification event  
Any comment:  Where  forest land  contains more  than one  forest  class,  the map must  be 
stratified into forest classes using Module X-STR.  
 
Data / Parameter:  Degradation PRA Results  
Source of data:  PRA  
Justification of choice of 
data  or   description  of 
measurement  methods 
and procedures applied:  
The PRA shall consist of semi-structured interviews / questionnaires.  
 
The  PRA  shall  evaluate  whether  timbe  harvest  (illegal  logging)  may  be 
occurring in the project area 
 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template

If ≥ 10% of those interviewed/surveyed believe that degradation may be 
occurring  within  the  project  boundary  then  the  limited  on-the-ground 
degradation survey shall be triggered  
 
An  additional  output  of  the  PRA  shall  be  a  depth  of  penetration  of 
degradation   pressure.   A   maximum   distance   shall   be   recorded   for 
penetration  into  the  forest  from  access  points  (such  as  roads,  rivers, 
already cleared areas) for the purpose of timber.  
 
It is likely that differing distances shall exist for each degradation pressure. 
If  multiple  pressures  exist  in  the  same  stratum  the  deepest  depth  of 
penetration shall be used to define Adeg,i  
 
Frequency: every two years  
Any comment:  Ex  ante,  an  estimation  shall  be  made  of  degradation  in  the  with-project 
case.  If  the  belief  is  that  zero  degradation  will  occur  within  the  project 
boundaries then this parameter may be set to zero if clear infrastructure, 
hiring and policies are in place to prevent deforestation.

APPENDIX 15: DATA AND PARAMETERS 
MONITORED FOR WRC 
 
 
Data/Parameter WTD
wps,i,j,t
 
Unit m 
Description Yearly average water table depth at stratum i, cell j, year t, in the project area, 
for use as a proxy in estimating CO2 emissions from microbial decomposition 
of peat soils 
Description of 
measurement 
methods and 
procedures to be 
applied:  
 
Spatial and temporal distributions of water table depths in a defined physical 
boundary of peatlands are the result of dynamics of water balance and follow 
established laws of physics. Measured water table depths distributed over 
several locations do not by themselves represent the average value(s) from 
the system, unless unrealistically large number of monitoring devices are in 
place, which makes it out of option for this project.  
Water balance modelling is a more appropriate method for estimating spatial 
and temporal distributions of water table depths. Measured water table 
depths from dipwells however can be used as useful initial information and 
indicative values, and, most importantly, as a source of data for model 
calibration. 
Water balance model for this project incorporates the following input-output 
system of water: 
- Daily rainfall (water input) 
- Daily evapotranspiration (water output) 
- Groundwater water flow (water output) 
- Overland flow (water output) 
- Open channel flow (water output) 
- Storage change (water balance) 
Governing model parameters/variables include: 
- Hydraulic conductivity of aquifer (peat soils) 
- DTM 
- Storage coefficient of aquifer 
- Aquifer thickness 
Boundary condition: 
- Water levels in canals 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
400 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
This water balance model uses the following sub-models: 
- Darcy for groundwater flow 
- Darcy-Weisbach for overland flow 
- Saint Venant for open channel flow 
Daily rainfall will be recorded by at least one rainfall station installed in the 
project area, and can be further enriched by using additional stations(s) 
outside project area, such as one from Rahadi Oesman Station in Ketapang. 
Measured water table depths (WTD
o
) will be provided by installing at least 50 
dipwells distributed over the project area. Water levels of existing canals will 
be measured by using at least 5 staff gauges. 
Hydraulic conductivity of peat soils will be sampled at least at 20 random 
locations by using auger hole (Van Bavel & Kirkham) method and/or inversed 
auger hole (Porchet) method. Storage coefficient will be sampled at least at 
20 random locations by using sample-core saturation method. 
This water balance model will be schematized with finite difference 
schematization and will be run in daily time-step. Model output includes water 
table heads (h) i.e., water table height above mean sea level. Modelled water 
table depths (WTD
m
) were calculated by subtracting DTM by h.  
 
For calibration purpose WTD
m
 will be compared against WTD
o
. Parameters 
storage coefficient, and/or hydraulic conductivity, and/or evapotranspiration 
will be optimized recursively, in such a way, with the objective of reducing 
RMSE between WTD
m
 and WTD
o
. We accept RMSE within 10 percent of WTD 
range. 
Final result of daily WTD
m
 will be averaged by year and can be used as a proxy 
for calculating CO2 emissions from microbial decomposition of peat soils. 
Frequency of 
recording 
Water table depths will be modelled in daily values and will be averaged by 
year. Measured water table depths for calibration will be recorded using 
manual dipwells with 2-weekly interval, and with automatic dipwells with 30-
minutes interval. 
Monitoring equipment -Manual dipwells use PVC perforated-screened case with millimeter scale rod 
-Automatic dipwells use PVC perforated-screened case with HOBO 20-L 
automatic water level logger 
-Manual staff gauges are custom-built using wooden rod and measuring scale 
-Automatic staff gauges use PVC perforated-screened case with HOBO 20-L 
automatic water level logger 
-Rainfall stations use Davis Weather Station 
Purpose of data Calculation of project emissions 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
401 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.4 
Calculation method NA 
QA/QC procedures to 
be applied 
Responsible staff will be trained well before carrying out any measurement 
campaign. SOP and standard data sheet will be provided and must be 
mastered by all operators.  
Crucial measurements will be documented with photos and/or videos. 
First-level QC will be performed by field supervisor to ensure appropriate entry 
and to identify obvious artefacts such as typos, misreading, etc. 
Second-level QC will be performed in Bogor for reassuring data quality by 
using manual/visual inspections, standard statistics, comparison between 
wells/stations, trend analysis, etc.
